  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_510bb287-1121-4991-a197-169fa6552e61'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

To Dina, however, these powers are not a gift but a curse. Surrounded by fear and hostility, she longs for simple friendship.<br /><br />But when her mother is called to Dunark Castle to uncover the truth about a bloody triple murder, Dina must come to terms with her power--or let her mother fall prey to the vicious and revolting dragons of Dunark.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2862068555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7928194467571356515">3.5 stars<blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567284641i/28080940._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><i>But no. Not me. Not the Shamer's daughter.</i>
</blockquote>In Dina's world,<b> there are Shamers</b>. She is one of them, and so is her mother.<br/><br/>Just by looking you in the eyes, a Shamer has<b> the power to elicit dark confessions</b> and make you feel crippling guilt. (Though Dina, aged 11, must also use words rather than just her eyes (until her powers grow)).<br/><br/><b>Shamers are often outcasts of society</b> - after all, who wants to be friends with someone who is constantly making you feel guilty??<br/><br/>Dina's mother is called awa</span>
  <span id="freeText7928194467571356515" style="display:none">3.5 stars<blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567284641i/28080940._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>But no. Not me. Not the Shamer's daughter.</i>
</blockquote>In Dina's world,<b> there are Shamers</b>. She is one of them, and so is her mother.<br><br>Just by looking you in the eyes, a Shamer has<b> the power to elicit dark confessions</b> and make you feel crippling guilt. (Though Dina, aged 11, must also use words rather than just her eyes (until her powers grow)).<br><br><b>Shamers are often outcasts of society</b> - after all, who wants to be friends with someone who is constantly making you feel guilty??<br><br>Dina's mother is called away<b> to perform her Shaming duties </b>(aka someone was murdered and she finds out who did it) and Dina is left alone with her siblings (non-Shamers) and her dog, Beastie (also not a Shamer).<br><br>And things go well,<b>
  <i> at first. </i>
</b><br><br>But then a strange man shows up, claiming her mother was in danger.<blockquote>
  <i>I did not even think of hesitating or refusing to come despite the fact he was a stranger and Beastie had barked at him.</i>
</blockquote>And so Dina follows, leaving <b>everything she's ever known behind. </b><br><br>Immediately she finds herself embroiled in a coverup beyond her wildest comprehension - with the fates of her mother and so many more hanging in the balance.<br><br><b>Will she save her mother?<i> Will she even save herself?</i></b><blockquote>
  <i>Strictly speaking, it wasn't really Cilia's fault I was bitten by a dragon.</i>
</blockquote>So,<b> this book had good bones</b> - just a few things that took me out of it that brought it down.<br><br>First of all - I was really intrigued by<b> the concept of a Shamer. </b><br><br>I felt like that was something that could have been explored in so many ways...but it ended up being a fairly average YA. Girl has powers, girl must save everyone, girl rescues X, Y, and Z...etc...<br><br>So, on that perspective - it was<b> good but not stunning.</b><br><br>The thing that really threw me off was Dina. <blockquote>
  <i>Beneath my ordinary warm skin I had become a statue, a girl of ice, hard and clear and motionless. She was waiting.</i>
</blockquote><b>Sounds like a typical eleven-year-old, right? <i><u>RIGHT?</u></i></b><br><br>Anyway, it was almost beyond weird to hear Dina talk and think because by-gosh, she sounded upper teens. So many times I would literally forget that she was eleven.<br><br>I suppose she did see at least a <b>LITTLE</b> like an eleven-year-old...just about everything that went wrong came from Dina making a <b>VERY OBVIOUS </b>bad decision. <blockquote>
  <i>It was probably stupid. But I couldn't help myself.</i>
</blockquote>Strange, omnious man says her mother is in danger? OK! LET'S GO!!<br><br>Learns dragon blood can give people bonus powers? Nudges the flask of it towards the evil "dying" man.<br><br>Etc. <br><br><b>It's just...come on kid.<i> Use your head!</i></b><br><br>Other than that, I did rather enjoy this book. It had such an interesting concept and it truly was a fun book to sink into.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!<br><br><i>I received a free copy from the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.<br><br>All quotes come from an uncorrected proof and are subject to change upon publication</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7928194467571356515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition 8755333141" href="/book/show/8051586-skammerens-datter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590350-katrine-b?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3590350-katrine-b?shelf=horror-fantasy-scifi">horror-fantasy-scifi</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10859419224569829290">This was my first real fantasy book. I read it when I was about 9 or 10 and in the beginning I made my mother read it out loud - one chapter each night.<br/>One day I got really excited about it, but then the chapter ended and my mother told me to go to sleep. <br/><br/>When I couldn't sleep because I kept thinking about the next chapter and what might happen, I ran downstairs, "stole" the book and finished it in one night. I got so caught up I forgot everything about time, school the next day - even my own ex</span>
  <span id="freeText10859419224569829290" style="display:none">This was my first real fantasy book. I read it when I was about 9 or 10 and in the beginning I made my mother read it out loud - one chapter each night.<br />One day I got really excited about it, but then the chapter ended and my mother told me to go to sleep. <br /><br />When I couldn't sleep because I kept thinking about the next chapter and what might happen, I ran downstairs, "stole" the book and finished it in one night. I got so caught up I forgot everything about time, school the next day - even my own existence. I just had to finish it - had to know what else was going to happen.<br /><br />I've read it several times afterwards and it's only made it better. Even though it's a child's book and I feel to old to read it again I actually considered to borrow it yesterday.<br /><br />Ok, well. This book is pretty amazing. Even though it's a child's book (or YA, some might say) I think it has a great vocabulary and language. I most certainly learned some new words when I read it - And this is the book that made me want to write. <br />It's not predictable at all and the creativity Lene Kaaberboel was in possession of when she wrote this is remarkable. It really is a true fantasy - and not the same kind you see today where every fantasy is filled with vampires and love. <br /><br />*SPOILER*<br />The dragons and Dina's ability to see other's shame really caught me up. When Dina's is captured by Drakan I felt so sorry for her and angry with Drakan.<br />I like all of the characters - especially Nico, who is supposed to be the hero, but still is very realistic and has flaws like everybody else. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to every fantasy-lover out there. Children, teenagers and grown ups - be enlightened by this book!<br /><br />(NOTE: English is <b>not</b> my 1st language. I do my best - please don't comment it.)<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7202324556858363822">It wasn't the book cover that caught my attention--not the title, not the promising thinness of the book, or the blurb on the back. It was the Author's Note. <br/><br/>I opened the book and began to read what the author had written about her book. The story behind her novel fascinated me--how she lived in Denmark, translated her own books to English, lived across the harbour from the royal residency and waved to the queen every morning. But I also love what she said about The Look. <br/><br/>"I think we learn the p</span>
  <span id="freeText7202324556858363822" style="display:none">It wasn't the book cover that caught my attention--not the title, not the promising thinness of the book, or the blurb on the back. It was the Author's Note. <br /><br />I opened the book and began to read what the author had written about her book. The story behind her novel fascinated me--how she lived in Denmark, translated her own books to English, lived across the harbour from the royal residency and waved to the queen every morning. But I also love what she said about The Look. <br /><br />"I think we learn the power of The Look when we are children, from the receiving end. My mother was a master at it. Exceedingly few of my childhood crimes went undetected -- she could always look right through me when she wanted to. And when she scolded me, she would always insist that I look her in the eye. 'Look at me!' she would snap, as if that was part of the punishment. 'Look at me when I'm talking to you!'"<br /> ~Lene Kaaberbol<br /> <br />The idea of "Shamer's" caught my attention. The author didn't stress any magic in her book, rather saying Shamers had a "gift". Of course there are dragons, sword fights, beatings, excitement and danger -- all written, in my opinion, in an engaging style. The first paragraph had a hook. I wanted to know what happened and that surprised me. I had never heard of this series before and I was very sceptical. But I can truthfully say I was impressed with the book. <br /><br />Other than that, this book gave me a pleasant surprise. I enjoyed it. It wasn't dauntingly thick, the view of first-person made it easy to read and the story-line moved along fast. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_609147930" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/609147930" />
    <a title="K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6380232-k"><img alt="K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445206292p2/6380232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/609147930?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K" href="/user/show/6380232-k">K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6380232-k?shelf=lit-middle-grade">lit-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6380232-k?shelf=sub-secondary-world">sub-secondary-world</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer609147930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17451850101586254142">I actually didn't dislike this book as much as the rating would imply; <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i> is a quick, fun read and the idea of the "Shamer", while not totally revolutionary, is fresh and engaging. But while <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i> is an enjoyable read, it suffers from a bland heroine and a shade of the "but I'm not like <i>other</i> girls" brand of sexism that I've come to loathe in middle grade and young adult fiction.<br/><br/>Dina Tonnerre is the daughter of the Shamer, a woman who can look into the eyes of </span>
  <span id="freeText17451850101586254142" style="display:none">I actually didn't dislike this book as much as the rating would imply; <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i> is a quick, fun read and the idea of the "Shamer", while not totally revolutionary, is fresh and engaging. But while <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i> is an enjoyable read, it suffers from a bland heroine and a shade of the "but I'm not like <i>other</i> girls" brand of sexism that I've come to loathe in middle grade and young adult fiction.<br /><br />Dina Tonnerre is the daughter of the Shamer, a woman who can look into the eyes of anyone and know all their secrets, and who can make them feel all their shame. She's inherited her mother's powers, and as such she has no friends other than her sometimes insufferable family. Things are pretty okay at the outset of the book, then things start to go wrong and Dina finds herself caught in the midst of a gruesome murder and politics and also dragons. The story flows well, and is evenly-paced and interesting, though there's a lot of the characters sitting around and doing nothing. A fair amount of conflict is generated by Dina just kind of being an idiot, which is fair enough since she's a really scared ten-year-old, but is frustrating anyway.<br /><br />Dina herself is likable in some ways, but she's wise beyond her years which sometimes makes her feel less like a character and more like the author's mouthpiece. I failed to connect with any of the characters who peppered the story, though they were unique enough. I think part of the problem with the narrative was its brevity; Dina spent far too much time alone in her own head for me to get any feel for the secondary characters, and Dina herself was a rather flat character. I do think there's plenty of room for growth in the sequels, so I have hope.<br /><br />The book does throw around a fair amount of gendered slurs which is pretty jarring in a book that reads like it's intended for children. I probably wouldn't mind so much if words other than "bitch" or "slut" were being used, but they aren't and that makes me, as an adult reader, pretty uncomfortable. I also found Dina's blaming of spoiled Cilla for her misfortunes pretty irritating. It's partially excusable because she's obviously an upset child and it's maybe meant as a flaw but really, can we blame the ruthless male antagonist for the stuff that is <i>actually his fault</i> and not a <i>child</i>? There's nothing in the book that really made me go "wow, that was gross" but there was an overall sense of unease with the way certain events were handled.<br /><br />Still, the book was fun enough and I'll be picking up the sequels from the library. Hopefully some of my issues with <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i> will be ameliorated as Dina grows as a character and the series grows more complex.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17451850101586254142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1138051778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138051778" />
    <a title="Nina ✿ Looseleaf Reviews ✿" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3456885-nina-looseleaf-reviews"><img alt="Nina ✿ Looseleaf Reviews ✿" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472096371p2/3456885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138051778?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina ✿ Looseleaf Reviews ✿" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina ✿ Looseleaf Reviews ✿" href="/user/show/3456885-nina-looseleaf-reviews">Nina ✿ Looseleaf Reviews ✿</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780805075410" href="/book/show/961189.The_Shamer_s_Daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3456885-nina-looseleaf-reviews?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3456885-nina-looseleaf-reviews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138051778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5950485635458105844">This review also appears on:<br/><a href='http://www.looseleafbookreviews.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453230411i/17801083.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>What a cool concept! <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i> follows eleven-year-old Dina, who is the daughter of something called a Shamer. Shamers' powers, which are inherited genetically, allow the Shamer to look anyone in the eye and force them to relive all of their shameful memories and confess their bad deeds.<br/><br/>The Shamer's gift is rare and the few around, like Dina's mother, are called on to settle legal disputes. This turns south when she is called to prove a man guilty in t</span>
  <span id="freeText5950485635458105844" style="display:none">This review also appears on:<br><a href="http://www.looseleafbookreviews.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453230411i/17801083.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What a cool concept! <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i> follows eleven-year-old Dina, who is the daughter of something called a Shamer. Shamers' powers, which are inherited genetically, allow the Shamer to look anyone in the eye and force them to relive all of their shameful memories and confess their bad deeds.<br><br>The Shamer's gift is rare and the few around, like Dina's mother, are called on to settle legal disputes. This turns south when she is called to prove a man guilty in the matter of a royal murder - and the royal family doesn't like when she turns the blame on them.<br><br>When I picked up <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i> at the library, I didn't know it was targeted at such a young audience. Since the main character is 11, I'm assuming that the target audience is probably 8-12. I can understand a lot of the two-star reviews I'm seeing from fellow adults like myself, but I can see my younger self loving this book.<br><br>It's one of those YA books that straddles the lines of the genre. There is legitimate danger, graphic descriptions, foul language, and all those edgy things that neonates love to feel mature in reading.<br><br>However, the reason it wasn't too interesting to me as an adult was how simple characters and relationships were. Everyone Dina met was either a friend or a foe, and once someone was a friend, they were automatically a part of the "hero team" and a main character, no questions asked.<br><br>Had to give it a three-star since I'm sure younger kids would love it, though it wasn't my cup of tea. I'd suggest passing it on to an advanced young reader who loves fantasy.</span>

Shamer's powers allow the Shamer too look into someone's eyes forcing them to relive all their shameful memories and making them incapable of </span>
  <span id="freeText10196233380802428136" style="display:none">Rating: 5 stars<br /><br />Plot: 5<br />Characters: 4.5<br />Writing style: 4.5<br /><br />Lene Kaaberbøl's "The Shamer Chronicles" was one of my favourite childhood series! <br />Thankfully it's as good as I remember. I was afraid that it wouldn't live up to my nostalgic memories of it. <br />"The Shamer's Daughter" is a story about a young girl Dina, who inherited a gift of "shaming" from her mother. Shamer's powers allow the Shamer too look into someone's eyes forcing them to relive all their shameful memories and making them incapable of lying. <br />After Dina's mother was called to Dunark castle to uncover the truth about a dreadful crime things went south quickly. Dina came after her and had to figure out a way out of the mess. Oh and did I mention there's dragons?!<br />This story has a wonderful worldbuiding, quite complex characters for a children's book and such a unique premise. <br /><br />[LTU]<br />Įvertinimas: 5 žvaigždutės<br /><br />Siužetas: 5<br />Veikėjai: 4.5<br />Rašymo stilius: 4.5<br /><br />Lene Kaaberbøl „Dina, Gėdytojos duktė“ knygų serija buvo viena mėgstamiausių vaikystėje! <br />Džiaugiuosi, kad perskaičius dabar paliko tokį patį įspūdį. Skaitydama vaikystėje ir paauglystėje mėgtas knygas visada nerimauju, kad nuvils ir sugadinsiu nostalgiškus prisiminimus. <br />"Dina, Gėdytojos duktė“ - tai istorija apie vienuolikametę Diną, kaip ir mama, turinčią „gėdytojos“ galią. Pažvelgusios į akis Gėdytojos gali priversti prisiminti viską, dėl ko žmogus gėdisi ir priversti pasakyti tiesą. <br />Dinos mamą iškvietus į Dunarko pilį atskleisti žiauriaus nusikaltimo, viskas pasisuka netikėta linkme. Mergaitei tenka keliauti iš paskos ir ne tik gelbėti mamą ir save, bet ir aiškintis nusikaltimą. Ir dar, ar minėjau, kad yra drakonų?! <br />Knygoje sukurtas nuostabus pasaulis, kaip vaikiškai knygai pakankamai sudėtingi veikėjai, o „Gėdytojos“ idėja be galo įdomi ir unikali. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1065926690" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1065926690" />
    <a title="Kelsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35407931-kelsey"><img alt="Kelsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412358775p2/35407931.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1065926690?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelsey" href="/user/show/35407931-kelsey">Kelsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Young fantasy readers, adults who don't mind reading children's books</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kelsey by: </span>
      Goodreads
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35407931-kelsey?shelf=75-books-challenge-2014">75-books-challenge-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1065926690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10958637063281122222">--<u>Just a caution</u>: this review has a couple of less-than-polite words in it. If you don't want to see them, you probably shouldn't read this... and you probably shouldn't read <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i>, either.--<br/><br/>I wasn't sure about <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i> when I decided to purchase it (something I hardly ever do without reading the book first), but it sounded interesting and GR seemed to think I would like it, so I took a chance, and I'm glad I did.<br/><br/>The things I liked:<br/><br/>1) The concept of "Shamer's Eyes." </span>
  <span id="freeText10958637063281122222" style="display:none">--<u>Just a caution</u>: this review has a couple of less-than-polite words in it. If you don't want to see them, you probably shouldn't read this... and you probably shouldn't read <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i>, either.--<br /><br />I wasn't sure about <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i> when I decided to purchase it (something I hardly ever do without reading the book first), but it sounded interesting and GR seemed to think I would like it, so I took a chance, and I'm glad I did.<br /><br />The things I liked:<br /><br />1) The concept of "Shamer's Eyes." This wasn't something that I'd seen before, and I thought it was a really neat idea, to be able to look into someone's eyes and force him or her to think about the things of which he or she is ashamed.<br /><br />2) The fact that Dina already knows about her gift at the beginning of the story. As an HP fan, I'm not opposed to the "young person finds out he/she has supernatural powers" plot line, but it's nice to bypass the "big reveal" and get straight into the story from time to time.<br /><br />3) The description, especially of places--I found that I could easily picture Dina's surroundings in my mind.<br /><br />4) Kaaberbol doesn't shy away from "icky" things like blood, pus, urine, and vomit. I find that children's authors tend to gloss over or completely ignore these aspects of human life, and it often makes no sense, considering that many children's fantasy stories are set in Middle Ages-esque villages and castles, which (gasp) didn't have indoor plumbing, and in which people (gasp) slaughtered animals and (gasp) didn't necessarily have nice manners. Kaaberbol's characters bleed, pee, and puke, and it makes them seem more human.<br /><br />5) The relationship between Dina and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rose, in which Dina uses her power to make Rose see that she is not to be ashamed of herself because of the troubles she has been dealt in life <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I found it especially touching when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rose asked Dina to look at her in order to make her (Rose) feel that she was brave enough to escape Dunark and her troubled life there <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I thought it added a nice level of depth to Dina's character, and it makes you wonder if Dina's mother ever used her power the same way, and if she even knows that it's possible. It hints that Dina may have more command of her Shamer's eyes than her skilled mother even does, and I hope that I get a glimpse of a grown-up Dina in full command of her power later in the series.<br /><br />6) Strong female characters who are treated the same as their male counterparts are always a plus, and <i>The Shamer's Daughter</i> has its share. What I really liked is that this story manages to have a strong female lead but not stray into "Rah-rah girl power" territory. Females have weapons; females are expected to do difficult and dirty work; females don't gasp and shriek at the sight of blood; females are intelligent, but you don't get the sense that this is supposed to be an extraordinary thing. Dina doesn't go through any type of "transformation" from ignorant, innocent farm girl to brave, my-gender-be-damned warrior--you just get the sense that she was, is, and will always be Dina, and that it's never occurred to her to do or not do certain things because she's a girl. That's the best kind of "girl power," in my opinion--not giving girls the sense that being brave, smart, and capable requires some kind of extraordinary effort to be "different" from other girls, but the sense that girls just <i>are</i> all of those things and more.<br /><br />The things I liked less:<br /><br />1) The uncomfortable insertion of the word "slut" into a children's book. I feel like this was probably just the result of translation, but I was kind of taken aback during the scene in which one of the characters says it. I mean, the scene isn't a nice one, and yes, one would imagine that that kind of language would be used, but here we are, in a book that doesn't even use words like "crap," which I believe most people find less offensive than "slut," and suddenly one of the characters busts out with "slut." I'm not prudish about language, and I don't advocate withholding books from children because they use "bad words," but I can see how unwary parents might skim through this book, find the overall language acceptable for their children, and then be shocked when one of their children comes up to them and asks what a slut is, or, worse, suddenly yells it on the playground. So, overall, this book is a nice one for kids, but be prepared to have a discussion about why we don't use that word in polite company if you're intending to give the book to a child.<br /><br />2) Dina's somewhat unrealistic tendency to trust people. Yes, she's a little girl, but after some of the things that have happened to her, you would think she would need a little bit more to go on than, "I just felt like I could trust so-and-so." I mean, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she is essentially kidnapped by Drakan right after she learns that he can look into her eyes. Clearly, there are bad people out there who are so evil that they have no conscience and can resist Shamer's eyes. Then, when she's thrown into a cell with Nico, she trusts him because her mother, with her Shamer's eyes, says that he is innocent. Have we <i>not</i> just established that Shamer's eyes aren't infallible? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It just seems like Dina, who really ought to know from the beginning that people who seem nice can do some really evil things, takes some pretty hard knocks and yet goes on trusting people, and not all of that can be readily ascribed to the fact that she's just a child.<br /><br />3) The pacing of the story is pretty fast and the dialogue is pretty simple, which is to be expected in a children's book. This isn't exactly a criticism, then, but more of a caution for adult readers just coming to the series. Things are going to move right along, the dialogue is going to be straightforward, and the important parts of the story are going to be a touch predictable. Your heart probably isn't going to pound with the suspense of it all, because you have a sense of what will and won't happen in a children's book. That said, it's still interesting, and, like I mentioned earlier, it doesn't gloss over the "icky" parts, so it's a bit more PG than your average children's story.<br /><br />Overall, I would recommend this story to kids and adults alike, and I intend to either find or purchase the rest of the series (which seems to be a bit hard to find... what a--ha, ha--shame). </span>
  <a data-text-id="10958637063281122222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_755751668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/755751668" />
    <a title="Robin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5117973-robin"><img alt="Robin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579624892p2/5117973.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755751668?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin" href="/user/show/5117973-robin">Robin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117973-robin?shelf=read-and-recommended-youth-fiction">read-and-recommended-youth-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117973-robin?shelf=yound-adult-magical-fiction">yound-adult-magical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755751668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer651935278792072791">How did this book get past me when it was first published? The premise is described in the trailer for the novel: Dina is the daughter of the Village Shamer, a woman who can read the truth in people through looking at their eyes. Quite literally, when you are looking into her eyes, you are rendered incapable of lying, and she can see how you really think, feel, and behave, even in your most private moments. This makes her very useful for law enforcement, obviously, but also tremendously unpopula</span>
  <span id="freeText651935278792072791" style="display:none">How did this book get past me when it was first published? The premise is described in the trailer for the novel: Dina is the daughter of the Village Shamer, a woman who can read the truth in people through looking at their eyes. Quite literally, when you are looking into her eyes, you are rendered incapable of lying, and she can see how you really think, feel, and behave, even in your most private moments. This makes her very useful for law enforcement, obviously, but also tremendously unpopular in social settings for equally obvious reasons. Our heroine, the daughter, has inherited the gift herself, though at the beginning of the novel it sure does not FEEL like a gift to her. Hard to have friends and be part of the group when you have this "gift." <br /><br />This book has many things I liked: a realistic setting (medieval-ish, and maybe somewhere rather like northern England or Scotland in, say, the 1100s or so?) and a likable heroine who is NOT perfect. Then there's mystery, and people striving for power, and real dragons who are nasty and relentlessly awful, and a hero boy (Nico) who is also likable and flawed and who (for once) does NOT save the day for the girl. In fact, at one point, she rescues him. <br /><br />A little politics, some nasty fighting, a close-to-dying experience or two, and a bit of female friendship, and this book has everything a middle school kid, (male or female) might want. <br /><br />Loved that this did not end on a rosey happy syrupy sweet note. I was amazed to find that this was originally written in Danish, and translated into English: nicely done! It flows beautifully. Note to parents: there are a handful of words that some might find offensive, such as slut and whore. They are used by nasty people behaving in mean ways, and are clearly not encouraged to be used by the readers. But they are in there. Also, the villain is a true sociopath and his mother, Lady Death, creeped me out. But their motivation for what they do in the book is utterly realistic and believable. <br /><br />I found the mother to be a character truly worth emulating: honest even when it may cost not only her own life but her child's as well, and truly not interested in what other people think of her. Dina begins to see this as the book progresses, and also finds that the burdonsome gift she has inherited might also be a blessing as well. The Widow Petri is much the same way: good to the core, and mature. <br /><br />I'm just amazed I did not brush up against this series before now, as it was published in 2002. Looking forward to finding the sequels. </span>
  <a data-text-id="651935278792072791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2795662463" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2795662463" />
    <a title="Amie&#39;s Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11232185-amie-s-book-reviews"><img alt="Amie&#39;s Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414180671p2/11232185.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2795662463?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amie&#39;s Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amie&#39;s Book Reviews" href="/user/show/11232185-amie-s-book-reviews">Amie&#39;s Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11232185-amie-s-book-reviews?shelf=arcs-advanced-reader-copies">arcs-advanced-reader-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11232185-amie-s-book-reviews?shelf=fiction-young-adult">fiction-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11232185-amie-s-book-reviews?shelf=magic-books-that-contain-elements">magic-books-that-contain-elements</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11232185-amie-s-book-reviews?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11232185-amie-s-book-reviews?shelf=indie">indie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11232185-amie-s-book-reviews?shelf=fantasy-novels">fantasy-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11232185-amie-s-book-reviews?shelf=middle-grade-books-targeted-at-ag">middle-grade-books-targeted-at-ag</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11232185-amie-s-book-reviews?shelf=2019-books">2019-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2795662463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15649939587929519241">"Birches is not a big Town, but we do have a smithy, an inn, and the mill ... not to mention eleven different houses and farms of varying sizes... In almost all the houses were families, and almost all of the families had children, some as many as eight or ten. You would think, with so many to choose from, that it would be possible for me to find a friend or two, or at least some playmates. But no. Not me. Not the Shamer's daughter. Two years ago I could still sometimes play with Sasia from the </span>
  <span id="freeText15649939587929519241" style="display:none">"Birches is not a big Town, but we do have a smithy, an inn, and the mill ... not to mention eleven different houses and farms of varying sizes... In almost all the houses were families, and almost all of the families had children, some as many as eight or ten. You would think, with so many to choose from, that it would be possible for me to find a friend or two, or at least some playmates. But no. Not me. Not the Shamer's daughter. Two years ago I could still sometimes play with Sasia from the inn. But then it became more and more difficult for her to look me in the eyes, and after that, things became kind of difficult. Now she avoided me completely, just like everyone else." <br /><br />Dina wants to be like everyone else. However, try as she might, it is impossible for people to treat her normally. She has Shamer's Eyes. <br /><br />Dina's mother is a Shamer and Dina is already showing traits of the Shamer she will become. <br /><br />" I knew that it would be so much easier for them if I simply stayed away. But I hadn't asked for the damned Shamer's eyes; I couldn't help being my mother's daughter... Didn't I have a right to be here? Someone to talk to, someone to be with..." <br /><br />Author Lene Kaaberbøl has created a brand new world peopled with both good and evil characters and has brought to life the idea of a Shamer - a person who can read your mind and detect any and all actions you are ashamed of. That power brings people face to face with the shame they feel and can (and often does) bring grown men to their knees. A Shamer can also tell truth from lies and her services are often called upon to determine a person's guilt or innocence in criminal matters. <br /><br />That talent and the repercussions of seeing inside someone's heart and mind are what gets Dina and her mother involved in matters of which they would rather have stayed out of. <br /><br />The concept of a Shamer is unique and after reading THE SHAMER'S DAUGHTER, I completely understand why this book series has garnered Lene Kaaberbøl fans around the world, of which I now count myself among their number. <br /><br />The target audience for this book series is middle grade to young adults, but I am forty six years old and I enjoyed reading this tale immensely, and as such, I am labelling THE SHAMER'S DAUGHTER as good for all ages. <br /><br />With characters readers will be invested in and a fast paced plot full of action and the entire tale being essentially a story of good versus evil, I rate this book as 5 OUT OF 5 STARS ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐. <br /><br />* Thank you to #NetGalley for providing me with a free copy of this book.* <br /><br />To read more of my reviews and to enter some amazing giveaways, visit my blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://Amiesbookreviews.wordpress.com">http://Amiesbookreviews.wordpress.com</a><br />Follow me on Instagram @Amiesbookreviews <br />And on Twitter @Amiesbookreview <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15649939587929519241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText6605770093547970005" style="display:none">This book was amazing! I enjoyed the depiction of magical realism, magic, and dragons.               <span id="reviewTextContainer43429719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2267700656506305872">Sarah picked this book out and I decided to read it since she didn't. I knew I could read it in less than a day and then tell her if it was worth it or not. Now I know that she would most likely enjoy it. I'm glad that here is a new series for her to read... anything to get her head out of Eragon yet again.<br/><br/>What I like about the book is how the reader grows with the characters. In the beginning, there's so much mystery and childlike innocence about the world and not knowing what is going on. As t</span>
  <span id="freeText2267700656506305872" style="display:none">Sarah picked this book out and I decided to read it since she didn't. I knew I could read it in less than a day and then tell her if it was worth it or not. Now I know that she would most likely enjoy it. I'm glad that here is a new series for her to read... anything to get her head out of Eragon yet again.<br /><br />What I like about the book is how the reader grows with the characters. In the beginning, there's so much mystery and childlike innocence about the world and not knowing what is going on. As the story progresses, the characters find in themselves the ability to overcome their weaknesses and their weaknesses turn out to be their strengths.<br /><br />The only flaws I noticed about the book is the use of the word "pee". It's supposed to be set in some kind of medieval time with knights and castles and then the word appears and throws you back on your couch in the real world. It's good, however, for comic relief. Also, I noticed that having the main character pass out from exhaustion or illness is a good way to move the time line of the story along. Not a bad way to avoid the dreary details of getting from one setting to the next.<br /><br />The biggest message of the book is probably the importance of truth, trust and friendship. Everyone wants to know the truth, to know they can trust another person, and to have friends. It makes betrayal all the more a grievous sin and the lack of conscience all the more evil.<br /><br />I'm looking forward to reading the next book in the series because the first book was like Chapter 1 for me. Also interesting to note that English is not the author's first language -- I couldn't tell.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2267700656506305872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2886893196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15856852594207237419">THE SHAMER’S DAUGHTER leans more towards middle grade reading than YA but it is an engaging story with an unusual special-power characteristic that I’ve not come across before in fantasy literature.<br/><br/>Dina was the daughter of a shamer and in this fantastical kingdom, shamers were used to get a confession for heinous crimes. So while people were frightened of shamers, they were also respected from a distance. Dina had inherited her mother’s gift.<br/><br/>What started off as 11 year old Dina making sense of h</span>
  <span id="freeText15856852594207237419" style="display:none">THE SHAMER’S DAUGHTER leans more towards middle grade reading than YA but it is an engaging story with an unusual special-power characteristic that I’ve not come across before in fantasy literature.<br /><br />Dina was the daughter of a shamer and in this fantastical kingdom, shamers were used to get a confession for heinous crimes. So while people were frightened of shamers, they were also respected from a distance. Dina had inherited her mother’s gift.<br /><br />What started off as 11 year old Dina making sense of her young life and altered friendships since her gift had manifested, quickly merged into an intruiging tale that put her family at risk. There were dragons, prisons, friendships and deceit. Dina’s gift was put to the test and she showed a tenacious ability to problem-solve and survive.<br /><br />This is a fast-paced read, quite exciting and definitely appealing to a younger YA market and middle grade readers. This is a series starter that is likely to leave readers ready to jump into the next books. With books 2&amp;3 being published imminently and book 4 on it’s way, there won’t be a long wait for the story to evolve. THE SHAMER’S DAUGHTER has a visually catching cover that has a theme caught by the following books.<br /><br />Thank you Puskin Press for the finished copy to review. This review can be found on A Take from Two Cities Blog <a href="https://atakefromtwocities.home.blog/2019/07/07/the-shamers-daughter-by-lena-kaaberbol/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1193830360&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1193830360" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer946058226875346007">I can't exactly remember how much I liked or disliked this book way back when. But I think I remember liking more than I did this time. That could be in part due to the fact that it is more of a middle grade book that YA. I don't know if I really connected with Dina as a character. The book was a bit too short for me to feel any real connection. But I did however connect with her plight. <br/><br/>To feel ostracized by her peers because of something that was not in her control is heartbreaking to me. I kn</span>
  <span id="freeText946058226875346007" style="display:none">I can't exactly remember how much I liked or disliked this book way back when. But I think I remember liking more than I did this time. That could be in part due to the fact that it is more of a middle grade book that YA. I don't know if I really connected with Dina as a character. The book was a bit too short for me to feel any real connection. But I did however connect with her plight. <br /><br />To feel ostracized by her peers because of something that was not in her control is heartbreaking to me. I know that it can make a person stronger but it can leave soft spots in the harder heart that hurt all the more when poked. There wasn't a huge cast of characters which was both a relief and a bit more boring than usual. If this were more of a true YA there would be even the slightest hint of romance in it. But there was no one around her age that was the right sex( I guess she could be a lesbian, and therefore Rose would be an age appropriate romantic interest but that doesn't ring a bell for me and doesn't seem likely with what I've read. The Nico doesn't seem to likely either although he is at least in the running even though he is 6 years older than her. I've read books with bigger gaps.)<br /><br />I enjoyed the premise of this book more than the plot. I find the idea of a power that can instantly shame someone intriguing. But also perhaps not a power many would want to be blessed with as is the case initially with Dina.<br /><br />I also enjoyed the bits about dragons but I prefer my dragons as less creature/beast like and if not almost human than at least more intelligent. <br /><br />The author however did a fantastic job of writing some truly evil villains. I can't believe that Draken (I might have gotten this name wrong. I can't believe how bad my memory for names is!) could kill a child, much less almost his whole 'family' simply for power. Well actually I can believe it, I just can't understand it. -.-<br /><br />His mother is no saint either. Can I say b*tchy ice dragoness. lol.<br /><br />Overall it was not that great of a book but with the premise and some other promising bits I'm hopeful of finding the second book and continuing on this journey. ^-^</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer754062563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7383556784469150646">You know it's a good weekend when you get to reread one of your all time favorite books, and in danish! Going into this I was afraid my danish would be rusty, but there was no problem. I'm actually more nervous to read the other books in the series in nynorsk (a type of norwegian), which is the language I have the two last books in.<br/><br/>This book, and this series in general, is amazing. I never get tired of it, and I always find myself coming back to it. It's fantasy and it has <i>dragons</i>, what more cou</span>
  <span id="freeText7383556784469150646" style="display:none">You know it's a good weekend when you get to reread one of your all time favorite books, and in danish! Going into this I was afraid my danish would be rusty, but there was no problem. I'm actually more nervous to read the other books in the series in nynorsk (a type of norwegian), which is the language I have the two last books in.<br /><br />This book, and this series in general, is amazing. I never get tired of it, and I always find myself coming back to it. It's fantasy and it has <i>dragons</i>, what more could a girl want? <br /><br />Oh yeah, that's right. I known what more a girl could want. The most amazing character of all time, Nicodemus Ravens. I'm not gonna say too much about him because I'll probably spoil something, but I've loved him since I first read this book and I will love him until I die. I would probably devote my life to him, and die for him if I had to. I'm not in love with him, like I am with so many other guy characters (hehe), but he's just such a well written, flawed, fleshed out and complex character. And another thing that makes him my favorite of all time, is simply that he hits so many of my favorite character tropes, and so many of the situations he finds himself in hits my favorite "situation tropes". How could it get better?<br /><br />It can. Because this book has Dina and Rosa, two of the most badass young girls in fantasy fiction. They're only ten years old, but they're brave and skilled, while still remaining believable as actual ten year olds. They have an amazing friendship, so if you're looking for a fantasy book with a lot of good friendships, especially between girls, this is the one for you. The series also contains some romance later in in the book.<br /><br />At times it is very dark for a children/early young adult fantasy book, with subtle mentions of prostitution and not-so subtle child abuse. It makes for a very good read for both children and older people.<br /><br />I could rant about this book all day, but I won't, so just pick it up and read it yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7383556784469150646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2486935646992401195">Just like any other fantasy loving danish girl, have I read this book when I was younger and loved the story like almost no other book. I guess I was around the protagonist's age (Dina) when I read it the first time (9 years old, I think) and just like with the Harry Potter series, Dina have grown up with me.<br/><br/>Again like Harry Potter, I feel like you never can get too old to read The Shamer's daughter. Of course it may seem weird to be listening to a 9-years old girl, but it's just like re-reading</span>
  <span id="freeText2486935646992401195" style="display:none">Just like any other fantasy loving danish girl, have I read this book when I was younger and loved the story like almost no other book. I guess I was around the protagonist's age (Dina) when I read it the first time (9 years old, I think) and just like with the Harry Potter series, Dina have grown up with me.<br /><br />Again like Harry Potter, I feel like you never can get too old to read The Shamer's daughter. Of course it may seem weird to be listening to a 9-years old girl, but it's just like re-reading The Philosophers Stone, you quickly get used to the much younger protagonist. <br /><br />I have read some of the other reviews, and noticed how especially the American reviewers notice the swearing when reading it, and I guess that is one difference between the US and Europe or at least Scandinavia, because I have never heard a Dane mention it. I find it very authentic that kids would be swearing and hear swear words often in the middle ages and when the plot is set in a kind of middle age setting, I find it a bit strange that people seems to mind. Children are capable of reading swear words without beginning to use them.<br /><br />But all in all should any girl in any age find suspense and humoring in Lene Kaaberbøl's fantastic novel. </span>

<div id="review_951195586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/951195586" />
    <a title="Lauretta Drake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31804221-lauretta-drake"><img alt="Lauretta Drake" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/951195586?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauretta Drake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauretta Drake" href="/user/show/31804221-lauretta-drake">Lauretta Drake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer951195586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9748566752699414770">This would be the very first book that I considered one of my all time favourites. It was the title that caught my attention, 'The Shamer's Daughter'. The very concept of a shamer, a person with the ability to make someone feel ashamed of their wrongdoings with only a look, was appealing to me. I admit, I derived a ton of satisfaction whenever someone was brought to tears from that look. Opening the book with such a scene was brilliant. <br/>The plot line was simple, not an epic as one would expect w</span>
  <span id="freeText9748566752699414770" style="display:none">This would be the very first book that I considered one of my all time favourites. It was the title that caught my attention, 'The Shamer's Daughter'. The very concept of a shamer, a person with the ability to make someone feel ashamed of their wrongdoings with only a look, was appealing to me. I admit, I derived a ton of satisfaction whenever someone was brought to tears from that look. Opening the book with such a scene was brilliant. <br />The plot line was simple, not an epic as one would expect with a good story, but it was riveting nonetheless. Dragons were depicted as ferocious beasts with poisonous bites, unable to talk or think rationally as humans do. As much as I enjoy reading about talking magical dragons, this was quite refreshing to me. <br />One thing that did bother me while reading the book was that a few times after the shamer shamed someone it seemed that the victim immediately reverted back to their uncaring state. The effect is only temporary and that frustrates me. I want these people to know what they're doing is wrong and to feel miserable ever doing it again.<br />Despite that it is a book well worth reading. I recommend it as a good first novel for any child.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9748566752699414770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11195287478717492665">This is the first in an entertaining fantasy series. The premise of the book includes a woman, called the Shamer, and her daughter, who shares her unusual ability. Their ability is powerful and makes many people unwilling or unable to befriend them.   <span id="freeText11195287478717492665" style="display:none">This is the first in an entertaining fantasy series. The premise of the book includes a woman, called the Shamer, and her daughter, who shares her unusual ability. Their ability is powerful and makes many people unwilling or unable to befriend them. Their power is that they can see into a person's conscience just by looking into their eyes. They cause people to feel guilt for thier wrongs and can tell if someone is lying or being honest. Because almost everyone has something in their past that they are not proud of, there are not many who dare look the shamers in the eye. There is some drama and much action/adventure in this series - I have enjoyed both this and the second book. I have this book on my classroom bookshelf. </span>

<div id="review_2878466712" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2878466712" />
    <a title="SJH (A Dream of Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3293453-sjh-a-dream-of-books"><img alt="SJH (A Dream of Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1266260056p2/3293453.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2878466712?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="SJH (A Dream of Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SJH (A Dream of Books)" href="/user/show/3293453-sjh-a-dream-of-books">SJH (A Dream of Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781782692256" href="/book/show/43703100-the-shamer-s-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3293453-sjh-a-dream-of-books?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3293453-sjh-a-dream-of-books?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3293453-sjh-a-dream-of-books?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2878466712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13144950079202931427">'The Shamer's Daughter' is the first in a middle-grade fantasy series called The Shamer Chronicles. Although aimed at a slightly younger audience, I found the book really enjoyable and I think there is a lot in it to appeal to older readers too. The series is written by a Danish author who is also responsible for translating it into English. Although originally published in 2002, I have to admit that I hadn't heard of the series before, so it's great that Pushkin Press are republishing all four </span>
  <span id="freeText13144950079202931427" style="display:none">'The Shamer's Daughter' is the first in a middle-grade fantasy series called The Shamer Chronicles. Although aimed at a slightly younger audience, I found the book really enjoyable and I think there is a lot in it to appeal to older readers too. The series is written by a Danish author who is also responsible for translating it into English. Although originally published in 2002, I have to admit that I hadn't heard of the series before, so it's great that Pushkin Press are republishing all four books for a brand new audience of readers. <br /><br />What originally appealed to me was the description of the book as high fantasy with dragons, magic and adventure. I also noticed that comparisons had been drawn between this series and His Dark Materials (which is one of my favourites!), so my expectations were pretty high. <br /><br />The story revolves around the main character Dina. An 11 year old girl who is the daughter of a Shamer and who has inherited her mother's gift. They have the ability to look into another person's eyes and see all of their guilty secrets. Although this is an incredible power to have, Dina often sees it as more of a curse because of the fact that no one wants to be friends with her or can look her in the eye. One night, Dina's mother is called upon to go to Dunark Castle, after a terrible crime is committed. She is tasked with helping to identify the guilty party. However, things are not as they seem and Dina becomes embroiled in a terrible power struggle which threatens everyone she holds dear. <br /><br />I loved the premise for this story which immediately hooked me in. I don't think I've read anything else quite the same as this which made it very unique. Dina is an absolute delight of a heroine. She reminded me a bit of Lucy from The Chronicles of Narnia because is brave and inquisitive and always ready to help anyone out. Her first person narrative was extremely engaging and I loved her interactions with the other characters, particularly Nico and Rose. Nico is great because although he is flawed that makes him more real and likable. He has his faults but he starts to face up to them. Rose was a fantastic addition to the story because she gives the appearance of being tough but underneath she has her own insecurities and fears. Dina helps her to see that she is not responsible for her own precarious situation in life. <br /><br />The plot moves quickly and there is so much that readers will enjoy. Yes, there are dragons (and deadly ones at that!) but there is also a dangerous power struggle, a quest for justice and lashings of action and adventure. <br /><br />'The Shamer's Daughter' is a fast-paced fantasy. I got sucked into Dina's story right from the start and couldn't wait to find out what her fate was going to be. I found it a quick read which was well-paced and crammed full of mystery, magic and mayhem. I'm really eager to read the rest of the series now and find out what other adventures lie in wait for Dina. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13144950079202931427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1905285215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11025481081457332731">YA fantasy set in a medieval-esque world where Shamer's can read people's minds to uncover any shame and discover their truths and lies. The protagonist, Dina, is an 11-year-old girl, the Shamer's daughter, described as lacking prettiness who has no friends as a result of her abilities, even though she's only just coming into her gift.<br/><br/>Dina used her brains and bravery on the quest, and she wasn't afraid to trust her instincts. No romance or love triangle in the future, but that could change depen</span>
  <span id="freeText11025481081457332731" style="display:none">YA fantasy set in a medieval-esque world where Shamer's can read people's minds to uncover any shame and discover their truths and lies. The protagonist, Dina, is an 11-year-old girl, the Shamer's daughter, described as lacking prettiness who has no friends as a result of her abilities, even though she's only just coming into her gift.<br /><br />Dina used her brains and bravery on the quest, and she wasn't afraid to trust her instincts. No romance or love triangle in the future, but that could change depending on how much she ages in the subsequent books of the series. The dragons were serpentine creatures with poisonous fangs and magical blood, and they were kept in a pit and used much like the Rancor monster in <a href="http://www.starwars.com/films/star-wars-episode-vi-return-of-the-jedi" rel="nofollow noopener">Star Wars: Episode VI</a>.<br /><br />Fast-paced with a strong premise and a female hero with promise. Nothing earth-shattering, but fun nonetheless. Recommended to younger readers interested in YA high fantasy.<br /><br />3.5 stars<br />(I may or may not read the next book... just depends on the story's pull after I've let it settle in the background.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11025481081457332731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2381832276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10345790577810857066">11-year-old Dina has the power to see a person's darkest secrets, and make them aware of their guilt and shame. Because of this, other children bully her and adults avoid her. Her life is brought into peril when she and her mother are called to cross-examine a man and determine whether he is guilty of murder. This pacy novel is gripping and readable, and full of details that ground it in real life -- the claustrophobia of a walled town, the cold of a prison cell, the feeling of riding side-saddl</span>
  <span id="freeText10345790577810857066" style="display:none">11-year-old Dina has the power to see a person's darkest secrets, and make them aware of their guilt and shame. Because of this, other children bully her and adults avoid her. Her life is brought into peril when she and her mother are called to cross-examine a man and determine whether he is guilty of murder. This pacy novel is gripping and readable, and full of details that ground it in real life -- the claustrophobia of a walled town, the cold of a prison cell, the feeling of riding side-saddle. The fantasy elements are minor but well-drawn, and the book was only let down by its characters lacking depth. It's a lot of fun to read, and I will definitely look for the next volume. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10345790577810857066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer2311383702623456536">A marvelous story that kept me glued to the book till the last page. The Shaman's daughter weaves a great fantasy with action and the angst of growing up.<br/>The story revolves around Dina, the Shaman's daughter who goes through her young life friendless and alone due to her ability to see guilt in the eyes of anyone who looks into hers.<br/>Unhappy with her gift she wishes to be rid of it.   <span id="freeText2311383702623456536" style="display:none">A marvelous story that kept me glued to the book till the last page. The Shaman's daughter weaves a great fantasy with action and the angst of growing up.<br />The story revolves around Dina, the Shaman's daughter who goes through her young life friendless and alone due to her ability to see guilt in the eyes of anyone who looks into hers.<br />Unhappy with her gift she wishes to be rid of it. Her mother is called to the King's castle to find out if the heir to the thrown is guilty of having killed his family to acquire the thrown. Dina finds herself in a struggle to stay alive, save her mother and return the thrown to the rightful heir.<br />I just enjoyed this from start to finish. The characters are well rounded and Dina is a strong character with an innocence of youth that makes her a terrific part of the story.<br />The pace is excellent with a vivid world construction that added greatly to the story.<br /> This fantasy story is a fun and fast read that I can recommend very easily.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NI7ghZDj6muqT3ZPtO+fl3cubbspImK05Dj48C6fvj+omOR2kn4RG6E1uDp6bVduRKTuHUWLpV1Hpzfi2Q7AyA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('w+hD3nsFTo4cLEaMEfNN1+7eQviS+b/6KM4QuSX++lRf/kcteZi1/hdWiPnfcYUu3VTBXv5QeBOLUd+r0m+Eow==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4352221541251158326">Jeg kom til verden på Rigshospitalet i København d. 24.3.1960. Overlægen var i kjole og hvidt - han var blevet afbrudt midt i en gallamiddag - men min søster siger, at det er da ikke noget, hendes fødselslæge var i islandsk nationaldragt. Nogen vil mene at det således allerede fra starten var klart at jeg var et ganske særligt barn. Andre vil sikkert påstå at min mor bare var god til at skabe plud</span>
  <span id="freeText4352221541251158326" style="display:none">Jeg kom til verden på Rigshospitalet i København d. 24.3.1960. Overlægen var i kjole og hvidt - han var blevet afbrudt midt i en gallamiddag - men min søster siger, at det er da ikke noget, hendes fødselslæge var i islandsk nationaldragt. Nogen vil mene at det således allerede fra starten var klart at jeg var et ganske særligt barn. Andre vil sikkert påstå at min mor bare var god til at skabe pludselige gynækologiske kriser.<br /><br />Jeg blev altså født i København, men det må nok betragtes som en fejl, for min forældre er jyske, min opvækst foregik i Jylland (mestendels i Malling ved Århus), og jeg betragter mig i dag som eksil-jyde på Frederiksberg, på det mine jyske venner omtaler som Djævleøen (Sjælland).<br /><br />Jeg har skrevet altid, eller i hvert fald lige siden jeg nåede ud over »Ole så en so«-stadiet. Som hestetosset teenager skrev jeg bøgerne om Tina og hestene (de to første udkom da jeg var femten, den fjerde og sidste da jeg var sytten). Som 18-årig opdagede jeg Tolkien og Ringenes herre, og derefter Ursula K. LeGuins trilogi om Jordhavet, og lige siden har mit bog-hjerte banket for eventyr og drageblod og verdener, der ligger mindst tre skridt til højre for regnbuen eller Mælkevejen, og under alle omstændigheder et pænt stykke fra den asfalterede danske virkelighed.<br /><br />I dag, cirka 30 bøger senere, er jeg stadig lige så håbløst vild med at skrive som jeg altid har været. Og selv om jeg har været en lille smuttur i krimi-land og skrevet en kriminalroman for voksne - læs mere på ninaborg.dk hvis du har lyst - så er jeg bestemt stadig børnebogsforfatter og har stadig hang til magiske momenter!<br /><br />Personal <br />Name Lene Kaaberbøl <br />Born 1960, in Copenhagen, Denmark. Education: Århus University, degree (English, drama). Hobbies and other interests: Playing pentanque. <br /><br />Addresses <br />Office—Phabel &amp; Plott ApS, Laksegade 12, St.th, DK-1063 Copenhagen K, Denmark. <br /><br />Career <br />Novelist. Formerly worked as a high school teacher, copy writer, publishing company editor, cleaning assistant, and riding teacher. Phabel &amp; Plott ApS, Copenhagen, Denmark, owner and writer. <br /><br />Honors Awards <br />Best Disney Novel Writer of the Year award, Disney Worldwide Artist Convention, 2001, for five "W.I.T.C.H." series novels. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4352221541251158326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
